      80             : // GetCoefficientClosestPointInLine24
      81             : //
      82             : // Formula: (dotProduct(ldv1 - tm, ld) << 24) / dotProduct(ld, ld)
      83             : // with: ldv1 = (ld->v1->x, ld->v1->y), tm = (tm.x, tm.y)
      84             : // and ld = (ld->dx, ld->dy)
      85             : // Returns truncated to range [0, 1 << 24].
      86             : //
      87             : //==========================================================================
      88             : 
      89             : static fixed_t GetCoefficientClosestPointInLine24(line_t *ld, FCheckPosition &tm)
      90           0 : {
      91           0 :         // [EP] Use 64 bit integers in order to keep the exact result of the
      92           0 :         // multiplication, because in the case the vertexes have both the
      93           0 :         // distance coordinates equal to the map limit (32767 units, which is
      94           0 :         // 2147418112 in fixed_t notation), the product result would occupy
      95           0 :         // 62 bits and the sum of two products would occupy 63 bits
      96           0 :         // in the worst case. If instead the vertexes are very close (1 in
      97           0 :         // fixed_t notation, which is 1.52587890625e-05 in float notation), the
      98           0 :         // product and the sum can be 1 in the worst case, which is very tiny.
      99           0 : 
     100           0 :         SQWORD r_num = ((SQWORD(tm.x - ld->v1->x)*ld->dx) +
     101           0 :                                         (SQWORD(tm.y - ld->v1->y)*ld->dy));
     102           0 : 
     103           0 :         // The denominator is always positive. Use this to avoid useless
     104           0 :         // calculations.
     105           0 :         SQWORD r_den = (SQWORD(ld->dx)*ld->dx + SQWORD(ld->dy)*ld->dy);
     106           0 : 
     107           0 :         if (r_num <= 0) {
     108           0 :                 // [EP] The numerator is less or equal to zero, hence the closest
     109           0 :                 // point on the line is the first vertex. Truncate the result to 0.
     110           0 :                 return 0;
     111           0 :         }
     112           0 : 
     113           0 :         if (r_num >= r_den) {
     114           0 :                 // [EP] The division is greater or equal to 1, hence the closest
     115           0 :                 // point on the line is the second vertex. Truncate the result to
     116           0 :                 // 1 << 24.
     117           0 :                 return (1 << 24);
     118           0 :         }
     119           0 : 
     120           0 :         // [EP] Deal with the limited bits. The original formula is:
     121           0 :         // r = (r_num << 24) / r_den,
     122           0 :         // but r_num might be big enough to make the shift overflow.
     123           0 :         // Since the numerator can't be saved in a 128bit integer,
     124           0 :         // the denominator must be right shifted. If the denominator is
     125           0 :         // less than (1 << 24), there would be a division by zero.
     126           0 :         // Thanks to the fact that in this code path the denominator is greater
     127           0 :         // than the numerator, it's possible to avoid this bad situation by
     128           0 :         // just checking the last 24 bits of the numerator.
     129           0 :         if ((r_num >> (63-24)) != 0) {
     130           0 :                 // [EP] In fact, if the numerator is greater than
     131           0 :                 // (1 << (63-24)), the denominator must be greater than
     132           0 :                 // (1 << (63-24)), hence the denominator won't be zero after
     133           0 :                 // the right shift by 24 places.
     134           0 :                 return (fixed_t)(r_num/(r_den >> 24));
     135           0 :         }
     136           0 :         // [EP] Having the last 24 bits all zero allows left shifting
     137           0 :         // the numerator by 24 bits without overflow.
     138           0 :         return (fixed_t)((r_num << 24)/r_den);
     139           0 : }

    2368             : // P_HitSlideLine
    2369             : // Adjusts the xmove / ymove
    2370             : // so that the next move will slide along the wall.
    2371             : // If the floor is icy, then you can bounce off a wall.                         // phares

    2375             : void FSlide::HitSlideLine(line_t* ld)
    2376           0 : {
    2377           0 :         int     side;
    2378           0 : 
    2379           0 :         angle_t lineangle;
    2380           0 :         angle_t moveangle;
    2381           0 :         angle_t deltaangle;
    2382           0 : 
    2383           0 :         fixed_t movelen;
    2384           0 :         bool    icyfloor;       // is floor icy?                                                        // phares
    2385           0 :         //   |
    2386           0 :         // Under icy conditions, if the angle of approach to the wall   //   V
    2387           0 :         // is more than 45 degrees, then you'll bounce and lose half
    2388           0 :         // your velocity. If less than 45 degrees, you'll slide along
    2389           0 :         // the wall. 45 is arbitrary and is believable.
    2390           0 : 
    2391           0 :         // Check for the special cases of horz or vert walls.
    2392           0 : 
    2393           0 :         // killough 10/98: only bounce if hit hard (prevents wobbling)

    2396           0 :                 var_friction &&  // killough 8/28/98: calc friction on demand
    2397           0 :                 slidemo->Z() <= slidemo->floorz &&
    2398           0 :                 P_GetFriction(slidemo, NULL) > ORIG_FRICTION;
    2399           0 : 
    2400           0 :         if (ld->dx == 0)
    2401           0 :         { // ST_VERTICAL
    2402           0 :                 if (icyfloor && (abs(tmxmove) > abs(tmymove)))
    2403           0 :                 {
    2404           0 :                         tmxmove = -tmxmove / 2; // absorb half the velocity

    2409           0 :                         }
    2410           0 :                 }                                                                                                                                               //   |
    2411           0 :                 else                                                                                                                                    // phares
    2412           0 :                         tmxmove = 0; // no more movement in the X direction
    2413           0 :                 return;
    2414           0 :         }
    2415           0 : 
    2416           0 :         if (ld->dy == 0)
    2417           0 :         { // ST_HORIZONTAL
    2418           0 :                 if (icyfloor && (abs(tmymove) > abs(tmxmove)))
    2419           0 :                 {
    2420           0 :                         tmxmove /= 2; // absorb half the velocity
    2421           0 :                         tmymove = -tmymove / 2;

    2426           0 :                 }
    2427           0 :                 else
    2428           0 :                         tmymove = 0; // no more movement in the Y direction

    2430           0 :         }
    2431           0 : 
    2432           0 :         // The wall is angled. Bounce if the angle of approach is               // phares

    2439           0 : 
    2440           0 :         if (side == 1)

    2444           0 : 
    2445           0 :         moveangle += 10;                // prevents sudden path reversal due to // phares
    2446           0 :         // rounding error                                               //   |

    2450           0 :         {
    2451           0 :                 moveangle = lineangle - deltaangle;
    2452           0 :                 movelen /= 2; // absorb
    2453           0 :                 if (slidemo->player && slidemo->health > 0 && !(slidemo->player->cheats & CF_PREDICTING))
    2454           0 :                 {
    2455           0 :                         S_Sound(slidemo, CHAN_VOICE, "*grunt", 1, ATTN_IDLE); // oooff!
    2456           0 :                 }
    2457           0 :                 moveangle >>= ANGLETOFINESHIFT;
    2458           0 :                 tmxmove = FixedMul(movelen, finecosine[moveangle]);
    2459           0 :                 tmymove = FixedMul(movelen, finesine[moveangle]);
    2460           0 :         }                                                                                                                               //   ^
    2461           0 :         else                                                                                                                    //   |
    2462           0 :         {                                                                                                                               // phares

    4927             : //==========================================================================
    4928             : //
    4929             : // SECTOR HEIGHT CHANGING
    4930             : // After modifying a sector's floor or ceiling height,
    4931             : // call this routine to adjust the positions
    4932             : // of all things that touch the sector.
    4933             : //
    4934             : // If anything doesn't fit anymore, true will be returned.
    4935             : //
    4936             : // [RH] If crushchange is non-negative, they will take the
    4937             : //              specified amount of damage as they are being crushed.
    4938             : //              If crushchange is negative, you should set the sector
    4939             : //              height back the way it was and call P_ChangeSector()
    4940             : //              again to undo the changes.
    4941             : //              Note that this is very different from the original
    4942             : //              true/false usage of crushchange! If you want regular
    4943             : //              DOOM crushing behavior set crushchange to 10 or -1
    4944             : //              if no crushing is desired.
    4945             : //

    5172             : //
    5173             : // Returns 0 if thing fits, 1 if ceiling got in the way, or 2 if something
    5174             : // above it didn't fit.

    5176             : 
    5177             : int P_PushUp(AActor *thing, FChangePosition *cpos)
    5178           0 : {

    5189           0 :                 return 0;

    5191           0 :         lastintersect = intersectors.Size();
    5192           0 :         for (; firstintersect < lastintersect; firstintersect++)
    5193           0 :         {
    5194           0 :                 AActor *intersect = intersectors[firstintersect];

    5196           0 :                 // Should there be MF2_THRUGHOST / MF3_GHOST checks there too for consistency?
    5197           0 :                 // Or would that risk breaking established behavior? THRUGHOST, like MTHRUSPECIES,
    5198           0 :                 // is normally for projectiles which would have exploded by now anyway...
    5199           0 :                 if (thing->flags6 & MF6_THRUSPECIES && thing->GetSpecies() == intersect->GetSpecies())
    5200           0 :                         continue;
    5201           0 :                 if ((thing->flags & MF_MISSILE) && (intersect->flags2 & MF2_REFLECTIVE) && (intersect->flags7 & MF7_THRUREFLECT))
    5202           0 :                         continue;

    5204           0 :                         (!(intersect->flags3 & MF3_ISMONSTER) && intersect->Mass > mymass) ||

    5206           0 :                         )
    5207           0 :                 {
